					<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">American rapper and actor (born 1975)</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>

</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://50cent.com">50cent<wbr />.com</a></span></td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Curtis James Jackson III</b> (born July 6, 1975),<sup id="cite_ref-allmusicbio_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusicbio-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> known professionally as <b>50 Cent</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;n 1&#93;</a></sup> is an American rapper, actor, television producer, and businessman. Born in the <a href="/wiki/South_Jamaica,_Queens" title="South Jamaica, Queens">South Jamaica</a> neighborhood of <a href="/wiki/Queens" title="Queens">Queens</a>, Jackson began pursuing a musical career in 1996. In early 2000, he recorded his "debut" album <i><a href="/wiki/Power_of_the_Dollar" title="Power of the Dollar">Power of the Dollar</a></i> for <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Records" title="Columbia Records">Columbia Records</a>, however he was struck by nine bullets during a shooting in May of that year, causing its release to be cancelled and Jackson to be dropped from the label. In 2002, Jackson released the mixtape <i><a href="/wiki/Guess_Who%27s_Back%3F" title="Guess Who&#39;s Back?">Guess Who's Back?</a></i>, and was thereafter discovered by <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a> and signed to his label <a href="/wiki/Shady_Records" title="Shady Records">Shady Records</a>, under the aegis of <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Aftermath_Entertainment" title="Aftermath Entertainment">Aftermath Entertainment</a> and <a href="/wiki/Interscope_Records" title="Interscope Records">Interscope Records</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>His first major-label album <i><a href="/wiki/Get_Rich_or_Die_Tryin%27" title="Get Rich or Die Tryin&#39;">Get Rich or Die Tryin'</a></i> (2003), was released to critical and commercial acclaim. The album spawned the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> number one singles "<a href="/wiki/In_da_Club" title="In da Club">In da Club</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/21_Questions" title="21 Questions">21 Questions</a>" (featuring <a href="/wiki/Nate_Dogg" title="Nate Dogg">Nate Dogg</a>), and was certified <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">9× Platinum</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA). That same year, he founded <a href="/wiki/G-Unit_Records" title="G-Unit Records">G-Unit Records</a>, signing his G-Unit associates <a href="/wiki/Young_Buck" title="Young Buck">Young Buck</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lloyd_Banks" title="Lloyd Banks">Lloyd Banks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tony_Yayo" title="Tony Yayo">Tony Yayo</a>; prior to becoming the <i>de facto</i> leader of the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_hip_hop" title="East Coast hip hop">East Coast hip hop</a> group <a href="/wiki/G-Unit" title="G-Unit">G-Unit</a>. 50 Cent had similar commercial and critical success with his second album, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Massacre" title="The Massacre">The Massacre</a></i> (2005), which contained his third number-one single "<a href="/wiki/Candy_Shop" title="Candy Shop">Candy Shop</a>" (featuring <a href="/wiki/Olivia_(singer)" title="Olivia (singer)">Olivia</a>). He then adopted a lighter, <a href="/wiki/Pop_rap" title="Pop rap">pop rap</a> derivative tone for his third and fourth albums, <i><a href="/wiki/Curtis_(50_Cent_album)" title="Curtis (50 Cent album)">Curtis</a></i> (2007) and <i><a href="/wiki/Before_I_Self_Destruct" title="Before I Self Destruct">Before I Self Destruct</a></i> (2009)—which were met with stagnate commercial reception and mixed reviews—and aimed for a return to his roots with his fifth album, <i><a href="/wiki/Animal_Ambition" title="Animal Ambition">Animal Ambition</a></i> (2014). He executive-produced and starred in the television series <i><a href="/wiki/Power_(TV_series)" title="Power (TV series)">Power</a></i> (2014–2020) and is slated to produce its spin-offs.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>50 Cent has sold over 30&#160;million albums worldwide and won <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_50_Cent" title="List of awards and nominations received by 50 Cent">several awards</a>, including a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Awards" title="Grammy Awards">Grammy Award</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Awards" title="Primetime Emmy Awards">Primetime Emmy Award</a>, thirteen <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Music_Awards" title="Billboard Music Awards"><i>Billboard</i> Music Awards</a>, six <a href="/wiki/World_Music_Awards" title="World Music Awards">World Music Awards</a>, three <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards" title="American Music Awards">American Music Awards</a> and four <a href="/wiki/BET_Awards" title="BET Awards">BET Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> As an actor, Jackson appeared in the semi-autobiographical film <i><a href="/wiki/Get_Rich_or_Die_Tryin%27_(film)" title="Get Rich or Die Tryin&#39; (film)">Get Rich or Die Tryin'</a></i> (2005), the war film <i><a href="/wiki/Home_of_the_Brave_(2006_film)" title="Home of the Brave (2006 film)">Home of the Brave</a></i> (2006), and the crime thriller film <i><a href="/wiki/Righteous_Kill" title="Righteous Kill">Righteous Kill</a></i> (2008). <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> ranked 50 Cent as the 17th best rapper of all time on their '50 Greatest rappers' list (2023);<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> and named him the sixth top artist of the 2000s decade.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> ranked <i>Get Rich or Die Tryin'</i> and "<a href="/wiki/In_da_Club" title="In da Club">In da Club</a>" in its lists of the "100 Best Albums of the 2000s" and "100 Best Songs of the 2000s" at numbers 37 and 13, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>
<p>Jackson was born in the borough of <a href="/wiki/Queens" title="Queens">Queens</a>, New York City, and raised in its <a href="/wiki/South_Jamaica,_Queens" title="South Jamaica, Queens">South Jamaica</a> neighborhood<sup id="cite_ref-allmusicbio_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusicbio-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> by his mother Sabrina. A drug dealer, Sabrina raised Jackson until she died in a fire when Jackson was 8.<sup id="cite_ref-MSNBC_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MSNBC-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RS_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RS-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Jackson revealed in an interview that his mother was a lesbian.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> After his mother's death and his father's departure, Jackson was raised by his grandparents.<sup id="cite_ref-OMM_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OMM-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He began boxing at about age 11, and when he was 14, a neighbor opened a boxing gym for local youth. "When I wasn't killing time in school, I was sparring in the gym or selling crack on the strip," Jackson remembered.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> He sold crack during primary school.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> "I was competitive in the ring and hip-hop is competitive too&#160;... I think rappers condition themselves like boxers, so they all kind of feel like they're the champ."<sup id="cite_ref-MTV2_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV2-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At age 12, Jackson began dealing <a href="/wiki/Narcotic" title="Narcotic">narcotics</a> when his grandparents thought he was in after-school programs,<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> and brought guns and drug money to school. In the tenth grade, he was caught by <a href="/wiki/Metal_detector" title="Metal detector">metal detectors</a> at <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Jackson_High_School_(Queens)" title="Andrew Jackson High School (Queens)">Andrew Jackson High School</a>: "I was embarrassed that I got arrested like that&#160;... After I got arrested I stopped hiding it. I was telling my grandmother [openly], 'I sell drugs.'"<sup id="cite_ref-MTV_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Curtis_Jackson_mugshot_1994.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Curtis_Jackson_mugshot_1994.jpg/200px-Curtis_Jackson_mugshot_1994.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="136" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Curtis_Jackson_mugshot_1994.jpg/300px-Curtis_Jackson_mugshot_1994.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Curtis_Jackson_mugshot_1994.jpg/400px-Curtis_Jackson_mugshot_1994.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1565" data-file-height="1066" /></a><figcaption>His mugshot in 1994</figcaption></figure>
<p>On June 29, 1994, Jackson was arrested for selling four vials of cocaine to an undercover police officer. He was arrested again three weeks later, when police searched his home and found heroin, ten ounces of crack cocaine, and a <a href="/wiki/Starting_pistol" title="Starting pistol">starting pistol</a>. Although Jackson was sentenced to three to nine years in prison, he served six months in a <a href="/wiki/Boot_camp_(correctional)#United_States" title="Boot camp (correctional)">boot camp</a> and earned his <a href="/wiki/General_Educational_Development" title="General Educational Development">GED</a>. He has said that he did not use cocaine himself.<sup id="cite_ref-OMM_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OMM-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rapnewsdirect.com_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rapnewsdirect.com-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Jackson adopted the nickname "50 Cent" as a <a href="/wiki/Metaphor" title="Metaphor">metaphor</a> for change.<sup id="cite_ref-AOL_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AOL-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The name was inspired by <a href="/wiki/Kelvin_Martin" title="Kelvin Martin">Kelvin Martin</a>, a 1980s Brooklyn robber known as "50 Cent"; Jackson chose it "because it says everything I want it to say. I'm the same kind of person 50 Cent was. I provide for myself by any means."<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span></h2>
<h3><span id="1996.E2.80.932002:_Rise_to_fame.2C_shooting.2C_and_early_mixtapes"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1996–2002:_Rise_to_fame,_shooting,_and_early_mixtapes">1996–2002: Rise to fame, shooting, and early mixtapes</span></h3>
<p>Jackson began rapping in a friend's basement, where he used <a href="/wiki/Phonograph" title="Phonograph">turntables</a> to record over instrumentals.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> In 1996, a friend introduced him to <a href="/wiki/Jam_Master_Jay" title="Jam Master Jay">Jam Master Jay</a> of <a href="/wiki/Run%E2%80%93D.M.C." class="mw-redirect" title="Run–D.M.C.">Run-DMC</a>, who was establishing <a href="/wiki/Jam_Master_Jay_Records" class="mw-redirect" title="Jam Master Jay Records">Jam Master Jay Records</a>. Jay taught him how to count <a href="/wiki/Bar_(music)" title="Bar (music)">bars</a>, write <a href="/wiki/Refrain" title="Refrain">choruses</a>, structure songs, and make records.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Jackson's first appearance was on "<a href="/wiki/React_(Onyx_song)" title="React (Onyx song)">React</a>" with <a href="/wiki/Onyx_(hip_hop_group)" title="Onyx (hip hop group)">Onyx</a>, for their 1998 album <i><a href="/wiki/Shut_%27Em_Down_(album)" title="Shut &#39;Em Down (album)">Shut 'Em Down</a></i>. He credited Jam Master Jay for improving his ability to write <a href="/wiki/Hook_(music)" title="Hook (music)">hooks</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-MTV2_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV2-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> and Jay produced Jackson's first (unreleased) album.<sup id="cite_ref-RS_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RS-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> In 1999, after Jackson left Jam Master Jay, the platinum-selling producers <a href="/wiki/Trackmasters" title="Trackmasters">Trackmasters</a> signed him to <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Records" title="Columbia Records">Columbia Records</a>. They sent him to an <a href="/wiki/Upstate_New_York" title="Upstate New York">upstate New York</a> studio, where he produced thirty-six songs in two weeks;<sup id="cite_ref-MSNBC_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MSNBC-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> eighteen were included on his 2000 album, <i><a href="/wiki/Power_of_the_Dollar" title="Power of the Dollar">Power of the Dollar</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-50Cent_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50Cent-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Jackson founded Hollow Point Entertainment with former <a href="/wiki/G-Unit" title="G-Unit">G-Unit</a> member Bang 'Em Smurf.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Jackson's popularity began to grow after the successful, controversial underground single "<a href="/wiki/How_to_Rob" title="How to Rob">How to Rob</a>", which he wrote in a half-hour car ride to a studio.<sup id="cite_ref-AOL_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AOL-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Part5_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Part5-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> The track comically describes how he would rob famous artists. Jackson explained the song's rationale: "There's a hundred artists on that label, you gotta separate yourself from that group and make yourself relevant".<sup id="cite_ref-AOL_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AOL-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Rappers <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kurupt" title="Kurupt">Kurupt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sticky_Fingaz" title="Sticky Fingaz">Sticky Fingaz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Big_Pun" title="Big Pun">Big Pun</a>, <a href="/wiki/DMX_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="DMX (rapper)">DMX</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wyclef_Jean" title="Wyclef Jean">Wyclef Jean</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Wu-Tang_Clan" title="Wu-Tang Clan">Wu-Tang Clan</a> responded to the track,<sup id="cite_ref-Part5_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Part5-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Nas" title="Nas">Nas</a> invited Jackson to join him on his <i><a href="/wiki/Nastradamus" title="Nastradamus">Nastradamus</a></i> tour.<sup id="cite_ref-MTV3_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV3-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Although "How to Rob" was intended to be released with "<a href="/wiki/Thug_Love_(song)" title="Thug Love (song)">Thug Love</a>" (with <a href="/wiki/Destiny%27s_Child" title="Destiny&#39;s Child">Destiny's Child</a>), two days before he was scheduled to film the "Thug Love" music video, Jackson was shot and hospitalized.<sup id="cite_ref-dubcnn_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dubcnn-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On May 24, 2000, Jackson was attacked by a gunman outside his grandmother's former home in South Jamaica. After getting into a friend's car, he was asked to return to the house to get some jewelry; his son was in the house, and his grandmother was in the front yard.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Jackson returned to the back seat of the car, and another car pulled up nearby; an assailant walked up and fired nine shots at close range with a <a href="/wiki/9_mm_caliber" title="9 mm caliber">9mm</a> <a href="/wiki/Handgun" title="Handgun">handgun</a>. Jackson was shot in the hand, arm, hip, both legs, chest, and left cheek.<sup id="cite_ref-RS_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RS-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MTV_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TIME_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TIME-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> His facial wound resulted in a swollen tongue, the loss of a wisdom tooth and a slightly slurred voice;<sup id="cite_ref-MTV_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MTV3_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV3-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> his friend was wounded in the hand. They were driven to a hospital, where Jackson spent thirteen days. The alleged attacker, Darryl "Homicide" Baum, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Tyson" title="Mike Tyson">Mike Tyson</a>'s close friend and bodyguard,<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> was killed three weeks later.<sup id="cite_ref-SOHH_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SOHH-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Jackson recalled the shooting: "It happens so fast that you don't even get a chance to shoot back&#160;.... I was scared the whole time&#160;... I was looking in the rear-view mirror like, 'Oh shit, somebody shot me in the face! It burns, burns, burns.'"<sup id="cite_ref-MTV_23-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> In his autobiography, <i>From Pieces to Weight: Once upon a Time in Southside Queens</i>, he wrote: "After I got shot nine times at close range and didn't die, I started to think that I must have a purpose in life&#160;... How much more damage could that shell have done? Give me an inch in this direction or that one, and I'm gone".<sup id="cite_ref-OMM_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OMM-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Jackson used a <a href="/wiki/Walker_(mobility)" title="Walker (mobility)">walker</a> for six weeks and fully recovered after five months. When he left the hospital he stayed in the <a href="/wiki/Pocono_Mountains" title="Pocono Mountains">Poconos</a> with his girlfriend and son, and his workout regime helped him develop a muscular physique.<sup id="cite_ref-RS_15-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RS-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MTV_23-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the hospital Jackson signed a publishing deal with Columbia Records before he was dropped from the label and blacklisted by the recording industry because of his song, "<a href="/wiki/Ghetto_Qu%27ran_(Forgive_Me)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ghetto Qu&#39;ran (Forgive Me)">Ghetto Qu'ran</a>". Unable to work in a U.S. studio, he went to Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-TSG_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TSG-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Blender_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Blender-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> With business partner <a href="/wiki/Sha_Money_XL" title="Sha Money XL">Sha Money XL</a>, Jackson recorded over thirty songs for <a href="/wiki/Mixtape" title="Mixtape">mixtapes</a> to build a reputation. In a <a href="/wiki/HitQuarters" title="HitQuarters">HitQuarters</a> interview, Marc Labelle of <a href="/wiki/Shady_Records" title="Shady Records">Shady Records</a> <a href="/wiki/Artists_and_repertoire" title="Artists and repertoire">A&amp;R</a> said that Jackson used the mixtape circuit to his advantage: "He took all the hottest beats from every artist and flipped them with better hooks. They then got into all the markets on the mixtapes and all the mixtape DJs were messing with them."<sup id="cite_ref-hitquarters.com_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hitquarters.com-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Jackson's popularity increased, and in 2002 he released the mixtape <i><a href="/wiki/Guess_Who%27s_Back%3F" title="Guess Who&#39;s Back?">Guess Who's Back?</a></i>. He then released <i><a href="/wiki/50_Cent_Is_the_Future" title="50 Cent Is the Future">50 Cent Is the Future</a></i> backed by <a href="/wiki/G-Unit" title="G-Unit">G-Unit</a>, a mixtape revisiting material by <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a> and <a href="/wiki/Raphael_Saadiq" title="Raphael Saadiq">Raphael Saadiq</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50Cent_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50Cent-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2002.E2.80.932007:_Mainstream_breakthrough.2C_Get_Rich_or_Die_Tryin.27.2C_and_The_Massacre"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2002–2007:_Mainstream_breakthrough,_Get_Rich_or_Die_Tryin',_and_The_Massacre">2002–2007: Mainstream breakthrough, <i>Get Rich or Die Tryin'</i>, and <i>The Massacre</i></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:50_Cent_(Cropped).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/50_Cent_%28Cropped%29.jpg/150px-50_Cent_%28Cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="195" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/50_Cent_%28Cropped%29.jpg/225px-50_Cent_%28Cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/50_Cent_%28Cropped%29.jpg/300px-50_Cent_%28Cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="564" data-file-height="734" /></a><figcaption>50 Cent in 2006</figcaption></figure>
<p>In 2002, <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a> heard Jackson's <i><a href="/wiki/Guess_Who%27s_Back%3F" title="Guess Who&#39;s Back?">Guess Who's Back?</a></i> CD, received from Jackson's attorney (who was working with Eminem's manager, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Rosenberg_(music_manager)" title="Paul Rosenberg (music manager)">Paul Rosenberg</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-dubcnn_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dubcnn-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Impressed, Eminem invited Jackson to fly to <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a> and introduced him to <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-RS_15-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RS-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dubcnn_36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dubcnn-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> After signing a $1&#160;million record deal,<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Jackson released <i><a href="/wiki/No_Mercy,_No_Fear" title="No Mercy, No Fear">No Mercy, No Fear</a></i>. The mixtape featured one new track, "<a href="/wiki/Wanksta" title="Wanksta">Wanksta</a>", which appeared on Eminem's <i><a href="/wiki/Music_from_and_Inspired_by_the_Motion_Picture_8_Mile" class="mw-redirect" title="Music from and Inspired by the Motion Picture 8 Mile">8 Mile</a></i> soundtrack.<sup id="cite_ref-50Cent_31-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50Cent-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Jackson was also signed by <a href="/wiki/Violator_(company)" title="Violator (company)">Violator Management</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sha_Money_XL" title="Sha Money XL">Sha Money XL</a>'s Money Management Group.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>50 Cent released his debut album, <i><a href="/wiki/Get_Rich_or_Die_Tryin%27" title="Get Rich or Die Tryin&#39;">Get Rich or Die Tryin'</a></i> (described by <a href="/wiki/AllMusic" title="AllMusic">AllMusic</a> as "probably the most hyped debut album by a rap artist in about a decade"), in February 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> noted its "dark synth grooves, buzzy keyboards and a persistently funky bounce", with Jackson complementing the production in "an unflappable, laid-back flow".<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> It debuted at number one on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>, selling 872,000 copies in its first four days.<sup id="cite_ref-USA_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USA-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> The lead single, "<a href="/wiki/In_da_Club" title="In da Club">In da Club</a>" (noted by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Source" title="The Source">The Source</a></i> for its "blaring horns, funky organs, guitar riffs and sparse hand claps"),<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> set a <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> record as the most listened-to song in radio history within a week.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:GUnitBKK.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="Three men and a woman holding decorative elephants" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/GUnitBKK.JPG/220px-GUnitBKK.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/GUnitBKK.JPG/330px-GUnitBKK.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/GUnitBKK.JPG/440px-GUnitBKK.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Olivia_(singer)" title="Olivia (singer)">Olivia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lloyd_Banks" title="Lloyd Banks">Lloyd Banks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Young_Buck" title="Young Buck">Young Buck</a>, and 50 Cent (left to right) in Bangkok, February 2006</figcaption></figure>
<p><a href="/wiki/Interscope_Records" title="Interscope Records">Interscope</a> began funding and distributing for Jackson's label, <a href="/wiki/G-Unit_Records" title="G-Unit Records">G-Unit Records</a>, in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> He signed <a href="/wiki/Lloyd_Banks" title="Lloyd Banks">Lloyd Banks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tony_Yayo" title="Tony Yayo">Tony Yayo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Young_Buck" title="Young Buck">Young Buck</a> as members of <a href="/wiki/G-Unit" title="G-Unit">G-Unit</a>, and <a href="/wiki/The_Game_(rapper)" title="The Game (rapper)">The Game</a> was later signed in a <a href="/wiki/Joint_venture" title="Joint venture">joint venture</a> with Dr. Dre's <a href="/wiki/Aftermath_Entertainment" title="Aftermath Entertainment">Aftermath Entertainment</a>. 50 Cent executive produced Lloyd Banks's June 2004 debut studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hunger_for_More" title="The Hunger for More">The Hunger for More</a></i>, which achieved Platinum status in America. 50 Cent also contributed vocals to Lloyd Banks's hit single, "<a href="/wiki/On_Fire_(Lloyd_Banks_song)" title="On Fire (Lloyd Banks song)">On Fire</a>".  In March 2005, 50 Cent's second commercial album, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Massacre" title="The Massacre">The Massacre</a></i>, sold 1.14&#160;million copies in its first four days (the highest in an abbreviated sales cycle<sup id="cite_ref-USA_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USA-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>) and was number one on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 for six weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> He was the first solo artist with three singles in the <i>Billboard</i> top five in the same week with "<a href="/wiki/Candy_Shop" title="Candy Shop">Candy Shop</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Disco_Inferno_(50_Cent_song)" title="Disco Inferno (50 Cent song)">Disco Inferno</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/How_We_Do_(song)" title="How We Do (song)">How We Do</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> According to <i>Rolling Stone</i>, "50's secret weapon is his singing voice&#160;- the deceptively amateur-sounding tenor croon that he deploys on almost every chorus".<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> 50 Cent's video game, <i><a href="/wiki/50_Cent:_Bulletproof" title="50 Cent: Bulletproof">50 Cent: Bulletproof</a></i> was released in November 2005. 50 Cent portrays himself and provides his likeness and voice in the video game, with the video game also featuring music from his first two studio albums.
</p><p>After The Game's departure Jackson signed <a href="/wiki/Olivia_(singer)" title="Olivia (singer)">Olivia</a> and rap veterans <a href="/wiki/Mobb_Deep" title="Mobb Deep">Mobb Deep</a> to G-Unit Records, with <a href="/wiki/Spider_Loc" title="Spider Loc">Spider Loc</a>, <a href="/wiki/M.O.P." title="M.O.P.">M.O.P.</a>, <a href="/wiki/40_Glocc" title="40 Glocc">40 Glocc</a> and Young Hot Rod later joining the label, who all eventually departed the label.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Jackson expressed an interest in working with rappers other than G-Unit, such as <a href="/wiki/Lil_Scrappy" title="Lil Scrappy">Lil' Scrappy</a> of <a href="/wiki/BME_Recordings" class="mw-redirect" title="BME Recordings">BME</a>, <a href="/wiki/LL_Cool_J" title="LL Cool J">LL Cool J</a> of <a href="/wiki/Def_Jam_Recordings" title="Def Jam Recordings">Def Jam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mase" title="Mase">Mase</a> of <a href="/wiki/Bad_Boy_Records" title="Bad Boy Records">Bad Boy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Freeway_(rapper)" title="Freeway (rapper)">Freeway</a> of <a href="/wiki/Roc-A-Fella_Records" title="Roc-A-Fella Records">Roc-A-Fella</a>, and recorded with several.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2007.E2.80.932010:_Curtis.2C_sales_battle_with_Kanye_West.2C_and_Before_I_Self_Destruct"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2007–2010:_Curtis,_sales_battle_with_Kanye_West,_and_Before_I_Self_Destruct">2007–2010: <i>Curtis</i>, sales battle with Kanye West, and <i>Before I Self Destruct</i></span></h3>
<p>In September 2007, 50 Cent released his third album, <i><a href="/wiki/Curtis_(50_Cent_album)" title="Curtis (50 Cent album)">Curtis</a></i>, which was inspired by his life before <i>Get Rich or Die Tryin'</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> It debuted at number two on the <i>Billboard</i> 200, selling 691,000 copies during its first week.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> It sold behind <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Graduation_(album)" title="Graduation (album)">Graduation</a></i>, released the same day; the outcome of this highly-publicized sales battle between Jackson and West has been accredited to the commercial decline of the <a href="/wiki/Gangsta_rap" title="Gangsta rap">gangsta rap</a> and "bling era" style that previously dominated mainstream hip-hop.<sup id="cite_ref-Burney_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Burney-59">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On the September 10, 2008, episode of <i><a href="/wiki/Total_Request_Live" title="Total Request Live">Total Request Live</a>,</i> Jackson said his fourth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Before_I_Self_Destruct" title="Before I Self Destruct">Before I Self Destruct</a></i>, would be "done and released in November". He released "<a href="/wiki/Ok,_You%27re_Right" title="Ok, You&#39;re Right">Ok, You're Right</a>", produced by Dr. Dre for <i><a href="/wiki/Before_I_Self_Destruct" title="Before I Self Destruct">Before I Self Destruct</a></i>, on May 18, 2009, and was scheduled to appear in a fall 2009 episode of <a href="/wiki/VH1" title="VH1">VH1</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Behind_the_Music" title="Behind the Music">Behind the Music</a></i>. On September 3, 2009, Jackson posted a video <sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> for the Soundkillers' Phoenix-<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> produced track, "Flight 187", introducing his mixtape and book (<i><a href="/wiki/The_50th_Law" title="The 50th Law">The 50th Law</a></i>). The song, with lyrics inspiring speculation about tension between Jackson and Jay-Z, was a bonus track on the iTunes version of <i>Before I Self Destruct</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Before_I_Self_Destruct" title="Before I Self Destruct">Before I Self Destruct</a></i> was released on November 9, 2009.
</p>
<h3><span id="2010.E2.80.932015:_New_musical_directions.2C_new_business_ventures.2C_and_Animal_Ambition"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2010–2015:_New_musical_directions,_new_business_ventures,_and_Animal_Ambition">2010–2015: New musical directions, new business ventures, and <i>Animal Ambition</i></span></h3>
<p>In a <a href="/wiki/Contactmusic.com" title="Contactmusic.com">Contactmusic.com</a> interview, Jackson said he was working on a <a href="/wiki/Eurodance" title="Eurodance">Eurodance</a> album, <i>Black Magic</i>, inspired by European nightclubs: "First they played hip-hop which suddenly changed to uptempo songs, known as Eurodance".<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> He later said he had changed his next album to <i>The Return of the Heartless Monster</i> after writing different material when he returned home from <a href="/wiki/The_Invitation_Tour" title="The Invitation Tour">the Invitation Tour</a> in 2010, shelving <i>Black Magic</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> On September 3, Jackson supported Eminem on his and <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a>'s <a href="/wiki/The_Home_%26_Home_Tour" title="The Home &amp; Home Tour">The Home &amp; Home Tour</a>, performing "Crack A Bottle" with Eminem and Dr. Dre amid rumors of tension between Jackson and Dre.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He "recorded 20 songs to a whole different album concept" before putting them aside,<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> wanting his new album to have the "aggression" of <i>Get Rich or Die Tryin<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-mtv.co.uk_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mtv.co.uk-69">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Jackson tweeted that the album was "80 percent done" and fans could expect it in the summer of 2011. It was ultimately delayed a year due to disagreements with Interscope Records, with Jackson saying that he would release it in November 2011<sup id="cite_ref-hiphopdx1_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hiphopdx1-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> with a different title than <i>Black Magic</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-hiphopdx1_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hiphopdx1-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Eminem would appear on the album, and Jackson said he was working with new producers such as <a href="/wiki/Boi-1da" title="Boi-1da">Boi-1da</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alex_da_Kid" title="Alex da Kid">Alex da Kid</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-72">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cardiak" title="Cardiak">Cardiak</a>, who produced <a href="/wiki/Lloyd_Banks" title="Lloyd Banks">Lloyd Banks</a>' "Start It Up", confirmed that he produced a song for the upcoming album.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:50_Cent-4_(cropped).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/50_Cent-4_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-50_Cent-4_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/50_Cent-4_%28cropped%29.jpg/255px-50_Cent-4_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/50_Cent-4_%28cropped%29.jpg/340px-50_Cent-4_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="444" data-file-height="667" /></a><figcaption>50 Cent performing in 2011</figcaption></figure>
<p>Jackson released a song, "<a href="/wiki/Outlaw_(50_Cent_song)" title="Outlaw (50 Cent song)">Outlaw</a>", from his fifth album on the Internet on June 16, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> The single, produced by Cardiak, was released on <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a> on July 19<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> (although Jackson tweeted that it was not the album's first single).<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> The rapper planned to write a semi-autobiographical young-adult novel about bullying, different from his previous books which focused on his life and the rules of power. According to the book's publisher, the first-person novel (about a 13-year-old schoolyard bully "who finds redemption as he faces what he's done")<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> was scheduled for publication in January 2012.
</p><p>In a series of <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">tweets</a>, Jackson said that the delay of his fifth album was due to disagreements with Interscope Records,<sup id="cite_ref-hiphopdx1_71-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hiphopdx1-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> later suggesting that it would be released in November 2011 with his headphone line (<a href="/wiki/SMS_Audio" title="SMS Audio">SMS by 50</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-hiphopdx1_71-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hiphopdx1-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> He speculated to MTV News about not renewing his five-album contract with Interscope: "I don't know&#160;... It will all be clear in the negotiations following me turning this actual album in. And, of course, the performance and how they actually treat the work will determine whether you still want to stay in that position or not."<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On June 20, 2011, Jackson announced the release of <i>Before I Self Destruct II</i> after his fifth album.<sup id="cite_ref-hiphopdx.com_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hiphopdx.com-79">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Although he planned to shoot a music video for the fifth album's lead single, "I'm On It", on June 26<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> the video was never filmed.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Jackson told Shade45, "I did four songs in Detroit with Eminem. I did two with Just Blaze, a Boi-1da joint, and I did something with Alex da Kid. We made two that are definite singles and the other two are the kinds of records that we been making, more aimed at my core audience, more aggressive, more of a different kind of energy to it."<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> He released "Street King Energy Track #7" in September 2011 to promote Street King, his charity-based energy drink.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> An announcement that Jackson was shooting a music video for "Girls Go Wild", the fifth-album lead single featuring <a href="/wiki/Jeremih" title="Jeremih">Jeremih</a>, was made on September 28, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Jackson's fifth album, <i><a href="/wiki/Street_King_Immortal" title="Street King Immortal">Street King Immortal</a></i>, was initially scheduled for a summer 2012 release and postponed until November 13.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Disagreements with Interscope Records about its release and promotion led to its temporary cancellation. Its first <a href="/wiki/Promo_single" class="mw-redirect" title="Promo single">promo single</a>, "<a href="/wiki/New_Day_(50_Cent_song)" title="New Day (50 Cent song)">New Day</a>" with <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alicia_Keys" title="Alicia Keys">Alicia Keys</a>, was released on July 27. The song was produced by Dr. Dre, mixed by <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a> and written by 50 Cent, Alicia Keys, <a href="/wiki/Royce_da_5%279%22" title="Royce da 5&#39;9&quot;">Royce da 5'9"</a> and Dr. Dre. A solo version by Keys was <a href="/wiki/News_leak" title="News leak">leaked</a> by her husband, <a href="/wiki/Swizz_Beatz" title="Swizz Beatz">Swizz Beatz</a>. "<a href="/wiki/My_Life_(50_Cent_song)" title="My Life (50 Cent song)">My Life</a>", the album's second promo single (with Eminem and <a href="/wiki/Maroon_5" title="Maroon 5">Maroon 5</a> lead singer <a href="/wiki/Adam_Levine" title="Adam Levine">Adam Levine</a>), was released on November 26, 2012.
</p><p>In January 2014, Jackson said he planned to release <i><a href="/wiki/Animal_Ambition" title="Animal Ambition">Animal Ambition</a></i> in the first quarter of the year, followed by <i>Street King Immortal</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> On February 20, he left Shady Records, Aftermath Entertainment, and Interscope, signing with <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Distribution" class="mw-redirect" title="Caroline Distribution">Caroline</a> and <a href="/wiki/Capitol_Music_Group" title="Capitol Music Group">Capitol Music Group</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> According to Jackson, although he owed Interscope another album, he was released from his contract because of his friendship with Eminem and Dr. Dre: "I'm a special case and situation. It's also because of the leverage of having the strong relationships with Eminem and Dr. Dre. They don't want me to be uncomfortable. They value our friendship to the point that they would never want [to jeopardize] it over that little bit of money."<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>That day, he announced that <i>Animal Ambition</i> would be released on June 3<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> and released its first track. The song, "Funeral", was released with a video on Forbes.com. Produced by Jake One, it is a continuation of "50 Bars" from a previous album; two more tracks were scheduled for release on March 18.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/South_by_Southwest" title="South by Southwest">South by Southwest</a> in Austin, Texas, Jackson performed "<a href="/wiki/Hold_On_(50_Cent_song)" title="Hold On (50 Cent song)">Hold On</a>" from the new album.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> That song and "Don't Worry 'Bout It" were released with accompanying videos on March 18.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> According to Jackson, prosperity would be a theme of the album: "This project, I had to search for a concept, a really good concept, in my perspective, and that was prosperity. I outlined all the things that would be a part of prosperity, positive and negative [for <i>Animal Ambition</i>]."<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2015.E2.80.93present:_Street_King_Immortal.2C_bankruptcy.2C_and_departure_from_Interscope"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2015–present:_Street_King_Immortal,_bankruptcy,_and_departure_from_Interscope">2015–present: <i>Street King Immortal</i>, bankruptcy, and departure from Interscope</span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Dont_Be_Mike_With_50_Cent_(cropped).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Dont_Be_Mike_With_50_Cent_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-Dont_Be_Mike_With_50_Cent_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="302" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Dont_Be_Mike_With_50_Cent_%28cropped%29.jpg/255px-Dont_Be_Mike_With_50_Cent_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Dont_Be_Mike_With_50_Cent_%28cropped%29.jpg/340px-Dont_Be_Mike_With_50_Cent_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="539" data-file-height="958" /></a><figcaption>50 Cent in 2017</figcaption></figure>
<p>On May 14, 2015, Jackson revealed in an interview that the first single from <i>Street King Immortal</i>, would be previewed Memorial Day weekend and would likely be released in June.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Jackson released "Get Low" on May 20, 2015, as the intended first single from his sixth studio album, <i>Street King Immortal</i>. The song, <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_production" title="Hip hop production">produced</a> by Remo the Hitmaker, features vocals from fellow American rappers <a href="/wiki/2_Chainz" title="2 Chainz">2 Chainz</a> and <a href="/wiki/T.I." title="T.I.">T.I.</a>, as well as American singer <a href="/wiki/Jeremih" title="Jeremih">Jeremih</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> He announced bankruptcy on July 13, 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On March 31, 2017, Interscope Records released 50 Cent's final album for the label, a greatest hits album titled <i><a href="/wiki/Best_Of_(50_Cent_album)" class="mw-redirect" title="Best Of (50 Cent album)">Best Of</a></i>.
</p><p>In 2020, Jackson led the executive-producer duties for late rapper <a href="/wiki/Pop_Smoke" title="Pop Smoke">Pop Smoke</a>'s debut album, <i><a href="/wiki/Shoot_for_the_Stars,_Aim_for_the_Moon" title="Shoot for the Stars, Aim for the Moon">Shoot for the Stars, Aim for the Moon</a></i>, having been one of Pop Smoke's biggest inspirations. The album was released on July 3, 2020. Jackson curated the album, desiring to finish it after Pop had died. He contacted many of the artists involved, and also features on one of the album tracks, "<a href="/wiki/The_Woo" title="The Woo">The Woo</a>". The Woo also features vocals from fellow American rapper <a href="/wiki/Roddy_Ricch" title="Roddy Ricch">Roddy Ricch</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2020, it was reported that Jackson was producing two television series for <a href="/wiki/Starz" title="Starz">Starz</a>, an anthology about hip hop and a biographical drama about sports agent <a href="/wiki/Nicole_Lynn" title="Nicole Lynn">Nicole Lynn</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2021, he became one of the headliners of the music festival <i>Golden Sand</i> in <a href="/wiki/Riviera_Maya" title="Riviera Maya">Riviera Maya</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2021, Curtis Jackson moved to <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>. This was thought to be for lower taxes, no income tax, and for the rapper scene, as well as other ventures such as writing new screenplays. Also, Jackson, Horizon United Group, and Houston Independent School District began a partnership on a project that would help high school students learn the business skills that define successful entrepreneurship.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
While living in Houston, Curtis Jackson was in the process of writing screenplays for new crime shows.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In a July 2021 interview with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">The Independent</a></i>, 50 Cent confirmed that he had officially decided to shelve his <i>Street King Immortal</i> album after it spent a decade in <a href="/wiki/Development_hell" title="Development hell">development hell</a>. He even confirmed that he plans to release a completely new project.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2021, he was confirmed to be starring in the upcoming <i><a href="/wiki/Expend4bles" title="Expend4bles">Expend4bles</a></i> film.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the fall of 2021 Starz released "Black Mafia Family," a series based on two brothers in Detroit who ran a drug trafficking and money laundering operation from the mid-1980s until 2005. Jackson is the executive producer of the show, which is based on a true story.
</p><p>On February 13, 2022, 50 Cent was a surprise performer in the <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_LVI" title="Super Bowl LVI">Super Bowl LVI</a> halftime show,<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> receiving a <a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award_for_Outstanding_Variety_Special_(Live)" title="Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Variety Special (Live)">Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Variety Special (Live)</a> in September for <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_LVI_halftime_show" title="Super Bowl LVI halftime show">the performance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Artistry">Artistry</span></h2>
<p>Jackson cites <a href="/wiki/Boogie_Down_Productions" title="Boogie Down Productions">Boogie Down Productions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Big_Daddy_Kane" title="Big Daddy Kane">Big Daddy Kane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juice_Crew" title="Juice Crew">The Juice Crew</a>, <a href="/wiki/EPMD" title="EPMD">EPMD</a> and <a href="/wiki/KRS-One" title="KRS-One">KRS-One</a> as his rapping influences, while citing <a href="/wiki/LL_Cool_J" title="LL Cool J">LL Cool J</a> as an inspiration behind his writing of "<a href="/wiki/21_Questions" title="21 Questions">21 Questions</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Jackson also states that he drew influences from <a href="/wiki/Nas" title="Nas">Nas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rakim" title="Rakim">Rakim</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Notorious_B.I.G." title="The Notorious B.I.G.">The Notorious B.I.G.</a> while working on <i><a href="/wiki/Animal_Ambition" title="Animal Ambition">Animal Ambition</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_ventures">Business ventures</span></h2>
<p>Jackson has had a highly successful business career. He is financially invested in a highly diversified variety of industries. Jackson is now involved in artist and talent management, record, television, and film production, footwear, apparel, fragrances, liquor, video games, mobile apps, book publishing, headphones, along with health drinks and dietary supplements.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> His broad business and investment portfolio contains investments in a variety of sectors including real estate, financial market investments, mining, boxing promotion, vodka, fragrances, consumer electronics and fashion.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He established his own record label <a href="/wiki/G-Unit_Records" title="G-Unit Records">G-Unit Records</a> in 2003 following his mainstream success.<sup id="cite_ref-Records_Signs_with_Interscope_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Records_Signs_with_Interscope-116">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> In November 2003, he signed a five-year deal with <a href="/wiki/Reebok" title="Reebok">Reebok</a> to distribute a G-Unit Sneakers line for his <a href="/wiki/G-Unit_Clothing_Company" title="G-Unit Clothing Company">G-Unit Clothing Company</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> In an interview, Jackson said his businesses had a habit of doing well as he saw all of his ventures both past and present as revolving around his alter ego.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Jackson has also started a book publishing imprint, <a href="/wiki/G-Unit_Books" title="G-Unit Books">G-Unit Books</a> on January 4, 2007, at the <a href="/wiki/Time_Warner_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="Time Warner Center">Time Warner Building</a> in New York.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> He has written a number of books including a memoir, <i>From Pieces To Weight</i> in 2005 where it sold 73,000 copies in hardcover and 14,000 copies in paperback; a crime novel and a book with <a href="/wiki/Robert_Greene_(American_author)" title="Robert Greene (American author)">Robert Greene</a> titled <i><a href="/wiki/The_50th_Law" title="The 50th Law">The 50th Law</a></i>, an urban take on <i><a href="/wiki/The_48_Laws_of_Power" title="The 48 Laws of Power">The 48 Laws of Power</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kamelia_Angelova_and_Hilary_Lewis_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kamelia_Angelova_and_Hilary_Lewis-122">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> In November 2011, Jackson released 50 Cent's Playground, a <a href="/wiki/Young_adult_fiction" title="Young adult fiction">young adult fiction</a> novel about a bullied, violent boy and his gay mother.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>One of Jackson's first business ventures was a partnership with <a href="/wiki/Energy_Brands" title="Energy Brands">Glacéau</a> to create an <a href="/wiki/Enhanced_water" title="Enhanced water">enhanced water</a> drink called Formula 50. In October 2004, Jackson became a beverage investor when he was given a minority share in the company in exchange for becoming a spokesperson after learning that he was a fan of the beverage. The health conscious Jackson noted that he first learned of the product while at a gym in Los Angeles, and stated that "they do such a good job making water taste good". After becoming a minority shareholder and celebrity spokesperson, Jackson worked with the company to create a new grape flavored "Formula 50" variant of VitaminWater and mentioned the drinks in various songs and interviews. In 2007, <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">Coca-Cola</a> purchased Glacéau for $4.1&#160;billion and, according to <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i>, Jackson, who was a minority shareholder, earned $100&#160;million from the deal after taxes.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Though he no longer has an equity stake in the company, Jackson continues to act as a spokesperson for VitaminWater, supporting the product including singing about it at the <a href="/wiki/BET_Awards" title="BET Awards">BET Awards</a> and expressing his excitement over the company's continuing to allow his input on products.<sup id="cite_ref-USAToday_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USAToday-125">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>
He joined <a href="/wiki/Right_Guard" title="Right Guard">Right Guard</a> to introduce a <a href="/wiki/Body_spray" title="Body spray">body spray</a> (Pure 50 RGX) and endorsed Magic Stick condoms,<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> planning to donate part of their proceeds to increasing HIV awareness.<sup id="cite_ref-NYPost_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYPost-127">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> Jackson signed a multi-year deal with Steiner Sports to sell his memorabilia,<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> and announced plans for a dietary-supplement company in conjunction with his film <i>Spectacular Regret</i> in August 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Val_Kilmer_and_50_Cent.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="50 Cent, smiling during an interview" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Val_Kilmer_and_50_Cent.jpg/220px-Val_Kilmer_and_50_Cent.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Val_Kilmer_and_50_Cent.jpg/330px-Val_Kilmer_and_50_Cent.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Val_Kilmer_and_50_Cent.jpg/440px-Val_Kilmer_and_50_Cent.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a><figcaption>50 Cent with <a href="/wiki/Val_Kilmer" title="Val Kilmer">Val Kilmer</a> at the 2009 <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="American Music Award">American Music Awards</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>Jackson has founded two film production companies: <a href="/wiki/G-Unit_Films_and_Television_Inc." title="G-Unit Films and Television Inc.">G-Unit Films</a> in 2003 and <a href="/wiki/Cheetah_Vision" title="Cheetah Vision">Cheetah Vision</a> in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> Cheetah Vision produces low budget action thrillers for foreign film markets across the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Kamelia_Angelova_and_Hilary_Lewis_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kamelia_Angelova_and_Hilary_Lewis-122">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50_Cent&#39;s_Massive_Business_Empire_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50_Cent&#39;s_Massive_Business_Empire-133">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> When G-Unit Films folded, he focused on Cheetah Vision and the company obtained $200&#160;million in funding in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> In 2010, Jackson revived G-Unit Films, renaming the company to G-Unit Films and Television Inc.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> The company has joint ventures with <a href="/wiki/Will_Packer" title="Will Packer">Will Packer</a>'s production company Will Packer Productions and Universal Television. In over 18 months, Jackson has sold projects to six different networks. Among them was <i><a href="/wiki/Power_(TV_series)" title="Power (TV series)">Power</a></i>, a STARZ drama in which he not only co-stars but also serves as co-creator and executive producer. <i>Power</i> debuted in June 2014 and was renewed for a second season after one episode.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Jackson serves as a co-star, co-creator and executive television producer of the STARZ network drama where he signed a 2-year contract with representation coming from the <a href="/wiki/Agency_for_the_Performing_Arts" title="Agency for the Performing Arts">Agency for the Performing Arts</a>. Ratings have been a success for Starz. with the second-season premiere being the highest-ever season with 1.43 million people tuning in live.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> "Power" ended in 2020. Jackson is the executive producer of three of its spin-offs, "PowerBook II: Ghost," "PowerBook III: Raising Kanan," and "Powerbook IV: Force."
</p><p>In 2002, Jackson filed an application with the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Patent_and_Trademark_Office" title="United States Patent and Trademark Office">United States Patent and Trademark Office</a> to register the term "50 Cent" as a trademark for clothing, sound recordings, and live performances. The application was published in 2003, and registration issued in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> He has since filed for additional trademark registrations.
</p><p>In July 2011, Jackson launched a philanthropic initiative to provide food for one billion starving people in Africa by 2016, joining Pure Growth Partners to introduce <a href="/wiki/Street_King_(drink)" title="Street King (drink)">Street King</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> A portion of the proceeds from each Street King purchase would be used to provide a daily meal to an underprivileged child. The partnership coincides with Jackson's goal to feed a billion people in Africa during the next five years. "50 Cent and I share a common vision: to address the world's problems through smart and sustainable business models," said Chris Clarke, founder and CEO of Pure Growth Partners. "With the rampant starvation in Africa and hunger afflicting children worldwide, we need socially responsible businesses that affect real change now more than ever." Jackson said, "I'm inspired by Clarke's vision and innovative approaches to tackling serious issues. It's our mission with Street King to really change children's lives around the world."<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, he founded <a href="/wiki/SMS_Audio" title="SMS Audio">SMS Audio</a>, a consumer-electronics company selling Street by 50 headphones, pledging to donate a portion of their sales to charity.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> In April 2015, SMS announced new co-branding deals with Reebok and Marvel. It added those to existing partnerships with Walt Disney Parks, Lucasfilm's Star Wars, and Intel.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2014, Jackson became a minority shareholder in Effen Vodka, a brand of vodka produced in the Netherlands, when he invested undisclosed amount in the company Sire Spirits LLC.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-independent1_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-independent1-152">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> He currently<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (September 2019)">when?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> endorses the product via his live concert performances and social media. The rapper was asked to take part in two promotional bottle signings, one in Oak Creek and another in Sun Prairie. Jackson made an appearance at Liquor Warehouse in Syracuse, New York on April 25, 2015, where he reportedly sold 1,400 bottles (277 gallons) of Jackson's signature liquor brand. Liquor Warehouse's owner George Angeloro reportedly stocked 300 cases (1,800 bottles or 357 gallons) of Effen Vodka, which sells for $30 a bottle, prior to the event.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2014, Jackson signed a $78 million deal with FRIGO Revolution Wear, a luxury underwear brand. The joint venture is partnered between Jackson, basketball player <a href="/wiki/Carmelo_Anthony" title="Carmelo Anthony">Carmelo Anthony</a>, baseball player <a href="/wiki/Derek_Jeter" title="Derek Jeter">Derek Jeter</a> and Mathias Ingvarsson, the former president of mattress company <a href="/wiki/Tempur-Pedic" title="Tempur-Pedic">Tempur-Pedic</a>. Jackson became the chief fashion designer for the brands single pair of Frigo boxers.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> In April 2015, Jackson mulled investing in Jamaica, exploring foreign investment opportunities on the island when he met with some local officials and had ongoing discussions on investment opportunities in the Montego Bay resort area.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Investments">Investments</span></h3>
<p>Over the years, Jackson invested his earnings from music and celebrity endorsements in an array of privately controlled companies, real estate, and stocks and bonds.<sup id="cite_ref-Kamelia_Angelova_and_Hilary_Lewis_122-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kamelia_Angelova_and_Hilary_Lewis-122">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> A portion of his investments lost value during the <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%9308" class="mw-redirect" title="Financial crisis of 2007–08">2008 recession</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50_Cent&#39;s_Massive_Business_Empire_133-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50_Cent&#39;s_Massive_Business_Empire-133">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> In December 2008, he told the Canadian press that he had been affected by the recession, losing several million dollars in the stock market. Unable to sell his Connecticut mansion, Jackson postponed <i>Before I Self-Destruct</i> due to the severity of the economic downturn.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>His Farmington mansion located on 50 Poplar Hill Drive that he tried to sell for years filed for bankruptcy in Connecticut in 2015 listed an asking price for that property in 2012 at $10 million but was valued at $8.3 million in 2015. He first tried to sell the house in 2007 for $18.5 million, and dropped the price several times in the next five years, when it was on and off the market.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2011, Jackson reportedly made $10 million after using Twitter to promote a marketing company which he was part shareholder of. His endorsements company G Unit Brands Inc. revealed through a public SEC filing controls 12.9 per cent of H&amp;H Imports, which is a parent company of TV Goods – the firm responsible for marketing his range of headphones, Sleek by 50 Cent. Jackson bought stock in the company on November 30, 2010, a week after it offered buyers 180 million shares at 17 cents each. Jackson later made a stock recommendation on Twitter, causing its share value to rise from four cents to nearly 50 cents (32p) each, closing on Monday at 39 cents (25p). Jackson was later investigated by the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Securities_and_Exchange_Commission" title="U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission">Securities and Exchange Commission</a> for breaching securities laws following his tweet which may have constituted allegations of <a href="/wiki/Insider_trading" title="Insider trading">Insider trading</a> via his <a href="/wiki/Pump_and_dump" title="Pump and dump">Pump and dump</a> stock investment strategy.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2013, Jackson became a minority investor in Hang w/, a live video broadcasting mobile app used by dozens of celebrities to broadcast their daily activities and chat with fans. The app was downloaded more than 1 million times since its launch in March 2013 and had more than 1 million users as of February&#160;2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=50_Cent&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>. Other minority celebrity investors include former <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">NFL</a> player <a href="/wiki/Terrell_Owens" title="Terrell Owens">Terrell Owens</a> and record producer <a href="/wiki/Timbaland" title="Timbaland">Timbaland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mining_and_heavy_metals">Mining and heavy metals</span></h3>
<p>In 2008, Jackson visited a platinum, palladium and iridium mine shaft in South Africa, and met with South African billionaire <a href="/wiki/Patrice_Motsepe" title="Patrice Motsepe">Patrice Motsepe</a> in talks of purchasing an equity stake in the mine.<sup id="cite_ref-Kamelia_Angelova_and_Hilary_Lewis_122-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kamelia_Angelova_and_Hilary_Lewis-122">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> After his meeting with Motsepe, Jackson considered purchasing equity in the mine and launching his own line of 50 Cent branded platinum.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Boxing_promotion">Boxing promotion</span></h3>
<p>On July 21, 2012, Jackson became a licensed <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a> <a href="/wiki/Promoter_(entertainment)" title="Promoter (entertainment)">promoter</a> when he formed his new company, TMT (The Money Team). Licensed to promote in New York, he was in the process of being licensed in <a href="/wiki/Nevada" title="Nevada">Nevada</a> (where most major fights are held in the U.S.). A former amateur boxer, Jackson signed gold medalist and former featherweight champion <a href="/wiki/Yuriorkis_Gamboa" title="Yuriorkis Gamboa">Yuriorkis Gamboa</a> and middleweight Olympic medalist <a href="/wiki/Andre_Dirrell" title="Andre Dirrell">Andre Dirrell</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> On July 29, 2012, he and the boxer <a href="/wiki/Floyd_Mayweather_Jr." title="Floyd Mayweather Jr.">Floyd Mayweather, Jr.</a>, signed IBF featherweight champion <a href="/wiki/Billy_Dib" title="Billy Dib">Billy Dib</a>. They unveiled plans to challenge the box-office dominance of <a href="/wiki/Mixed_martial_arts" title="Mixed martial arts">mixed martial arts</a> and change the landscape of boxing with TMT Promotions.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> Boxer <a href="/wiki/Zab_Judah" title="Zab Judah">Zab Judah</a> also expressed interest in making a deal with Jackson.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> In December 2012, Mayweather and Jackson parted company, with Jackson taking over the promotion company and founding SMS Promotions<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> with Gamboa, Dirrell, Dib, <a href="/wiki/James_Kirkland_(boxer)" title="James Kirkland (boxer)">James Kirkland</a>, Luis Olivares and Donte Strayhorn in his stable.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bankruptcy">Bankruptcy</span></h4>
<p>On July 13, 2015, Jackson filed for <a href="/wiki/Chapter_11,_Title_11,_United_States_Code" title="Chapter 11, Title 11, United States Code">Chapter 11 bankruptcy</a> protection in the U.S. Bankruptcy Court for the District of Connecticut with a debt of $32,509,549.91.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> On July 17, 2015, the Court issued an order allowing a creditor to proceed with the punitive damages phase of a trial against Jackson in a New York state court, in connection with the alleged release of a private video.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> His assets were listed as between $10 million and $50 million in his bankruptcy petition, though he testified under oath that he is worth $4.4 million.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> Citing between $10 million and $50 million in debt, and the same amount in assets. Later in the week, Jackson's bankruptcy lawyers elucidated the court documents that legal fees and judgments exceeding $20 million over the past year were the primary cause of the filing.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>His filings listed 32 entities that he has a stake in. The bankruptcy came days after a jury ordered him to pay $5 million to rapper Rick Ross's ex-girlfriend Lastonia Leviston for invading her privacy by posting online a sex tape of her and another man.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> In addition, Jackson lost a dispute over a failed business deal to come to fruition to his Sleek headphones, where Jackson invested more than $2 million.<sup id="cite_ref-Gleason_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gleason-180">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> An ex-partner accused Jackson of later stealing the design of the "Sleek by 50" headphones, prompting a judge to award the partner more than $17.2 million.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> His Connecticut bankruptcy filing states that he owns seven cars valued at more than $500,000, including a 2010 Rolls-Royce and a 1966 <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet" title="Chevrolet">Chevrolet</a> Coupe.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> His expenses of $108,000 a month include $5,000 for gardening along with a monthly income of $185,000, mainly from royalties and income from his external businesses and investments. The court filing says he also owes money to his stylist, his barber, and his fitness coach.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Other details in the bankruptcy documents included information about two deals that sold the right to collect royalties of on-air play of his music.
