Half the rights to his portfolio were sold to the British independent music publishing company <a href="/wiki/Kobalt_Music_Group" title="Kobalt Music Group">Kobalt Music Group</a> for $3 million and the other half for another $3 million with the sales of his albums allowing Jackson to own 100 percent of the rights to the master recordings while paying only for distribution.<sup id="cite_ref-Stephanie_Gleason_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stephanie_Gleason-186">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> Zeisler &amp; Zeisler, a Bridgeport law firm, represented 50 Cent in the bankruptcy, which later resulted in Jackson filing a $75 million lawsuit against his own lawyers.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> He stated that his lawyers did a terrible job of representing him, specifically citing the fallout of his failed venture with Sleek Audio headphones and accused Garvey Schubert Barer, a Wall Street law firm, of failing to "employ the requisite knowledge and skill necessary to confront the circumstances of the case".<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gleason_180-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gleason-180">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_positions"><span class="anchor" id="Endorsements"></span>Corporate positions</span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/G-Unity_Foundation_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="G-Unity Foundation Inc.">G-Unity Foundation Inc.</a> – Founder</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/SMS_Audio" title="SMS Audio">SMS Audio</a><sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> – CEO, founder</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Street_King_(drink)" title="Street King (drink)">SK Energy</a><sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> – Founder</li>
<li>SMS Promotions<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> – CEO, founder</li>
<li>Sire Spirits<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> – Owner</li>
<li>Effen Vodka<sup id="cite_ref-independent1_152-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-independent1-152">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> – Former minority shareholder</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<p>On October 13, 1996, Jackson's girlfriend, Shaniqua Tompkins, gave birth to son Marquise.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> Tompkins later sued Jackson for $50&#160;million in 2009, saying he promised to take care of her for life. The suit, with 15 <a href="/wiki/Cause_of_action" title="Cause of action">causes of action</a>, was dismissed by a judge who called it "an unfortunate tale of a love relationship gone sour".<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> The two have bickered for years, and have even taken their feud to social media many times.<sup id="cite_ref-Bossip_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bossip-202">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Feud_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feud-203">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Marquise's birth changed Jackson's outlook on life: "When my son came into my life, my priorities changed, because I wanted to have the relationship with him that I didn't have with my father."<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> He credited his son for inspiring his career and being the "motivation to go in a different direction".<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> Despite this, the two have endured a fractured relationship that began when Jackson and Tompkins separated in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> Their feud has been taken to social media numerous times, including in 2020 when Jackson disclosed that he "used to" love his son.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> Jackson has a tattoo "Marquise" with an axe on his right biceps ("The axe is 'cause I'm a warrior. I don't want him to be one, though"),<sup id="cite_ref-Blender_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Blender-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> and has "50", "Southside" and "Cold World" on his back: "I'm a product of that environment. It's on my back, though, so it's all behind me".<sup id="cite_ref-Blender_43-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Blender-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2003, Jackson briefly dated actress <a href="/wiki/Vivica_A._Fox" title="Vivica A. Fox">Vivica A. Fox</a>. He broke up with her only 8 months later on the radio.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Jackson dated model Daphne Joy and had his second son, Sire Jackson, with her, on September 1, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> At the age of two years, Sire modeled for Kidz Safe, a headphone brand for kids, earning $700,000 through his contract.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2005, Jackson supported President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> after rapper <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a> criticized Bush for a slow response to the victims of <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Hurricane Katrina</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> If his felony convictions did not prevent him from voting, he said that he would have voted for the president.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> Jackson later said that Bush "has less compassion than the average human. By all means, I don't aspire to be like George Bush."<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> In September 2007, he told <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> that although he would not endorse a candidate in 2008, he "liked <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary [Clinton]</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Six months later, the rapper told <a href="/wiki/MTV_News" title="MTV News">MTV News</a> that he had switched his support to <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> after hearing him speak, but had lost interest in politics.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> Asked his opinion of President Obama's May 9, 2012, endorsement of <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage" title="Same-sex marriage">gay marriage</a>, Jackson said, "I'm for it&#160;... I've encouraged same-sex activities. I've engaged in fetish areas a couple times."<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> He had been criticized for anti-gay comments in the past.<sup id="cite_ref-glaad_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-glaad-220">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Despite having numerous songs that reference drug and alcohol usage, Jackson remains <a href="/wiki/Teetotal" class="mw-redirect" title="Teetotal">teetotal</a>, citing a bad experience with alcohol as his main reason.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> noted Jackson's wealth in 2007, ranking him second behind <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a> in the rap industry.<sup id="cite_ref-Hip-Hop_Cash_Kings_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hip-Hop_Cash_Kings-225">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> He lived in a <a href="/wiki/Farmington,_Connecticut" title="Farmington, Connecticut">Farmington, Connecticut</a>, mansion formerly owned by ex-boxer <a href="/wiki/Mike_Tyson" title="Mike Tyson">Mike Tyson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> Jackson listed the mansion for sale in 2007 at $18.5 million to move closer to his son (who lived on <a href="/wiki/Long_Island" title="Long Island">Long Island</a> at the time).<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> The mayor of <a href="/wiki/Bridgeport,_Connecticut" title="Bridgeport, Connecticut">Bridgeport, Connecticut</a>, declared October 12, 2007 "50 Cent Curtis Jackson Day", honoring the rapper with a proclamation and a <a href="/wiki/Key_to_the_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Key to the City">key to the city</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> One of Jackson's New York homes, purchased in January 2007 for $2.4&#160;million and the center of a lawsuit between Jackson and Shaniqua Tompkins, caught fire on May 31, 2008, while he was filming in Louisiana.<sup id="cite_ref-chicagotribune.com_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chicagotribune.com-229">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2008, he told the Canadian press that he had lost several million dollars in the stock market and, unable to sell his Connecticut mansion, had postponed <i>Before I Self-Destruct</i> because of the economic downturn.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> Jackson won a lawsuit in November 2009 against <a href="/wiki/Taco_Bell" title="Taco Bell">Taco Bell</a> over the fast-food chain's use of his name without permission.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Jackson endorsed Democratic candidate <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a> in the run-up for the 2016 U.S. presidential election.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup> He rejected an offer of $500,000 from the Trump campaign to make an appearance on the candidate's behalf.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> However, he endorsed <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> in 2020, due to his dislike of <a href="/wiki/Joe_Biden" title="Joe Biden">Joe Biden</a>'s tax plans.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup> A week later, he retracted his endorsement, saying on Twitter "Fu*k Donald Trump, I never liked him",<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> and endorsed Biden.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_issues">Legal issues</span></h3>
<p>On June 29, 1994, Jackson was arrested for selling four vials of <a href="/wiki/Cocaine" title="Cocaine">cocaine</a> to an undercover police officer. He was arrested again three weeks later, when police searched his home and found <a href="/wiki/Heroin" title="Heroin">heroin</a>, ten ounces of <a href="/wiki/Crack_cocaine" title="Crack cocaine">crack cocaine</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Starting_pistol" title="Starting pistol">starter's pistol</a>. Although Jackson was sentenced to three to nine years in prison, he served six months in a <a href="/wiki/Boot_camp_(correctional)" title="Boot camp (correctional)">boot camp</a> (where he earned his high-school equivalency diploma). According to him, he did not use cocaine.<sup id="cite_ref-OMM_18-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OMM-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rapnewsdirect.com_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rapnewsdirect.com-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Jackson and four members of his entourage were arrested shortly before 2&#160;a.m. on December 31, 2002, when police found a .25-caliber handgun and a .45-caliber pistol in a parked car (which they searched due to its tinted windows) outside a Manhattan nightclub. The rapper was charged with two counts of criminal possession of a weapon.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Jackson was sentenced to two years' <a href="/wiki/Probation" title="Probation">probation</a> on July 22, 2005, for a May 2004 incident, when he was charged with three counts of <a href="/wiki/Assault" title="Assault">assault</a> and <a href="/wiki/Battery_(crime)" title="Battery (crime)">battery</a> after jumping into an audience when he was hit by a water bottle.<sup id="cite_ref-crime.about.com_239-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crime.about.com-239">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lawsuits">Lawsuits</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Use_of_image">Use of image</span></h4>
<p>Jackson filed a lawsuit against an advertising company, Traffix of <a href="/wiki/Pearl_River,_New_York" title="Pearl River, New York">Pearl River, New York</a>, on July 21, 2007, for using his image in a promotion he said threatened his safety. He was alerted by a staff member to an Internet advertisement on a <a href="/wiki/Myspace" title="Myspace">Myspace</a> page. According to court documents, the advertisement had a cartoon image of the rapper with "Shoot the rapper and you will win $5000 or five ring tones guaranteed". Although the ad did not use his name, the image allegedly resembled him and suggested that he endorsed the product. The lawsuit, calling the ad a "vile, tasteless and despicable" use of Jackson's image which "quite literally call[ed] for violence against him", sought unspecified <a href="/wiki/Punitive_damages" title="Punitive damages">punitive damages</a> and a permanent injunction against the use of his image without permission.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Use_of_name">Use of name</span></h4>
<p>In 2008, Jackson sued <a href="/wiki/Taco_Bell" title="Taco Bell">Taco Bell</a> over an ad campaign in which it invited him to change his name for one day from 50 Cent to 79 Cent, 89 Cent, or 99 Cent, in line with pricing for some of its items, and they would donate $10,000 to the charity of his choice. The case was settled out of court.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Janitor_incident">Janitor incident</span></h4>
<p>While walking through <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati/Northern_Kentucky_International_Airport" title="Cincinnati/Northern Kentucky International Airport">Cincinnati/Northern Kentucky International Airport</a> in May 2016, Jackson harassed and insulted a janitor at the airport, accusing him of being <a href="/wiki/Altered_state_of_consciousness" title="Altered state of consciousness">under the influence</a>. The janitor was a hearing-impaired, <a href="/wiki/Autistic" class="mw-redirect" title="Autistic">autistic</a> teenager named Andrew Farrell. The parents of the janitor had seen the viral video as disrespect and wanted to sue Jackson for his action against their child. The lawsuit was originally over one million dollars, but the parents settled for a $100,000 donation to <a href="/wiki/Autism_Speaks" title="Autism Speaks">Autism Speaks</a> and his apology.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bamba_sample">Bamba sample</span></h4>
<p>In 2016, a judge declared that Brandon Parrott gave Dr. Dre and 50 Cent the rights to "Bamba" for the song "P.I.M.P."<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_civil_and_criminal_matters">Other civil and criminal matters</span></h3>
<p>One of his New York homes, purchased for $2.4&#160;million in January 2007 and the center of a lawsuit between Jackson and Shaniqua Tompkins, caught fire on May 30, 2008, while he was filming in Louisiana.<sup id="cite_ref-chicagotribune.com_229-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chicagotribune.com-229">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> On August 5, 2013, Jackson pleaded not guilty to one count of domestic violence and four counts of vandalism in a Los Angeles County court. If convicted of all charges, he faced up to five years in prison and a $46,000 fine. Model-actress Daphne Joy accused Jackson of kicking her and ransacking her bedroom during an argument at her condominium in the Toluca Lake neighborhood of Los Angeles on June 23. He allegedly caused $7,100 in property damage, leaving the scene before police arrived.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Judge Ann Nevins has ordered Jackson back to court because of Instagram messages he made over several months.<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup> She said Jackson was not fully clear about his funds and indicated posts of the rapper showing stacks of his money. In March 2016, Jackson claimed that he would no longer use <a href="/wiki/Instagram" title="Instagram">Instagram</a>, electing instead to have his profile page operated by someone else.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2020, Jackson was a subject of controversy for his involvement in a viral video of him giving money to a <a href="/wiki/Burger_King" title="Burger King">Burger King</a> restaurant in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> on behalf of a local scammer who was later arrested and charged for <a href="/wiki/Bitcoin" title="Bitcoin">Bitcoin</a> scamming and for assaulting and kidnapping his victims on April 24, 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Feuds">Feuds</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ja_Rule">Ja Rule</span></h3>
<p>Before he signed with Interscope Records, Jackson engaged in a public dispute with rapper <a href="/wiki/Ja_Rule" title="Ja Rule">Ja Rule</a> and his label, <a href="/wiki/Murder_Inc._Records" title="Murder Inc. Records">Murder Inc. Records</a>, saying that a friend robbed jewelry from Ja Rule and the latter accused him of orchestrating the robbery.<sup id="cite_ref-Playboy_256-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Playboy-256">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup> Ja Rule said that the conflict stemmed from a Queens video shoot, when Jackson did not like seeing him "getting so much love" from the neighborhood.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/The_Hit_Factory" title="The Hit Factory">The Hit Factory</a> in New York in March 2000, Jackson had an altercation with Murder Inc. associates and received three stitches for a stab wound.<sup id="cite_ref-Playboy_256-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Playboy-256">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup> Rapper <a href="/wiki/Black_Child_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="Black Child (rapper)">Black Child</a> claimed responsibility for the stabbing, saying that he acted in self-defense when he thought someone reached for a gun.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>An <a href="/wiki/Affidavit" title="Affidavit">affidavit</a> by an <a href="/wiki/Internal_Revenue_Service" title="Internal Revenue Service">Internal Revenue Service</a> (IRS) agent suggested ties between Murder Inc. and <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_McGriff" title="Kenneth McGriff">Kenneth "Supreme" McGriff</a>, a New York drug lord suspected of involvement in the murder of <a href="/wiki/Jam_Master_Jay" title="Jam Master Jay">Jam Master Jay</a> and Jackson's shooting. An excerpt read:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The investigation has uncovered a conspiracy involving McGriff and others to murder a rap artist who has released songs containing lyrics regarding McGriff's criminal activities. The rap artist was shot in 2000, survived and thereafter refused to cooperate with law enforcement regarding the shooting. Messages transmitted over the Murder Inc. pager indicate that McGriff is involved in an ongoing plot to kill this rap artist, and that he communicates with Murder Inc. employees concerning the target.<sup id="cite_ref-TSG_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TSG-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>The end of the Jackson-Ja Rule feud was confirmed in May 2011. According to Ja Rule, "I'm cool. We ain't beefing no more. We'll never collaborate. That's just what it is. You don't have to be at war with somebody, but it's also kind of like U.S. and another country that they may not get along with. We don't gotta go to war, but we're not friends either. But we can coincide inside of a world. He's doing him, and he's not thinking about me, and I'm doing me and I'm not thinking about him."<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On August 7, 2015, the feud between the two rappers later reignited when Ja Rule gave a feedback to a social follower via Twitter over a similar feud between <a href="/wiki/Meek_Mill" title="Meek Mill">Meek Mill</a> and <a href="/wiki/Drake_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="Drake (rapper)">Drake</a>. Enraged, Jackson later responded with photos and comments via Instagram, only siding with Drake.<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup> The feud resurfaced three years later on January 19, 2018, when Ja Rule took to Twitter, calling out 50 Cent on social media.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Game">The Game</span></h3>
<p>Although Jackson was close to <a href="/wiki/The_Game_(rapper)" title="The Game (rapper)">The Game</a> before the latter released his debut album, <i>The Documentary</i>, they grew apart. After <i>The Documentary</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s release, Jackson felt that The Game was disloyal for saying that he did not want to participate in G-Unit's feuds with other rappers (such as <a href="/wiki/Nas" title="Nas">Nas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jadakiss" title="Jadakiss">Jadakiss</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fat_Joe" title="Fat Joe">Fat Joe</a>) and his desire to work with artists with which G-Unit was feuding. He said that he wrote six songs for the album and did not receive proper credit, which The Game denied.<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:50_cent_in_concert.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="Black-and-white closeup of 50 Cent singing onstage" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/50_cent_in_concert.jpg/220px-50_cent_in_concert.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/50_cent_in_concert.jpg/330px-50_cent_in_concert.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/50_cent_in_concert.jpg/440px-50_cent_in_concert.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="533" /></a><figcaption>50 Cent at a 2007 concert</figcaption></figure>
<p>Jackson later dismissed The Game from G-Unit on <a href="/wiki/WQHT" title="WQHT">Hot 97</a>. After the announcement, The Game (a guest earlier in the evening) tried to enter the building with his entourage. After they were denied entry, one of his associates was shot in the leg in a confrontation with a group of men leaving the building.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup> When the situation escalated, the rappers held a joint press conference announcing their reconciliation,<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup> and fans were uncertain if the rappers had staged a publicity stunt to boost sales of their recently released albums.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup> After the situation cooled,<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup> G-Unit criticized The Game's <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/street_credibility" class="extiw" title="wikt:street credibility">street credibility</a> and announced that they would not appear on his albums. During a <a href="/wiki/Summer_Jam_(festival)" title="Summer Jam (festival)">Summer Jam</a> performance The Game announced a <a href="/wiki/Boycott" title="Boycott">boycott</a> of G-Unit, which he called "G-Unot".<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After the Summer Jam performance The Game recorded "300 Bars and Runnin'", an extended "diss" of G-Unit and Roc-A-Fella Records, for the mixtape <i>You Know What It Is Vol. 3</i>. Jackson responded with his "<a href="/wiki/Piggy_Bank_(song)" title="Piggy Bank (song)">Piggy Bank</a>" music video, with The Game as <a href="/wiki/Mr._Potato_Head" title="Mr. Potato Head">Mr. Potato Head</a> and parodies of other rivals.<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup> They have continued attacking each other, with The Game releasing two more mixtapes: <i>Ghost Unit</i> and a mixtape-DVD, <i><a href="/wiki/Stop_Snitchin,_Stop_Lyin" title="Stop Snitchin, Stop Lyin">Stop Snitchin, Stop Lyin</a></i>. Jackson superimposed The Game's head on the body of a male stripper for the cover of the <i>Hate It or Love It (G-Unit Radio Part 21)</i> mixtape in response to The Game's pictures of G-Unit dressed as the <a href="/wiki/Village_People" title="Village People">Village People</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup> The Game, under contract to Aftermath Entertainment, signed with <a href="/wiki/Geffen_Records" title="Geffen Records">Geffen Records</a> to terminate his contractual obligations with G-Unit (although it is claimed that Jackson pressured Dr. Dre to fire him).<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup> G-Unit member <a href="/wiki/Spider_Loc" title="Spider Loc">Spider Loc</a> has insulted The Game in songs, and the latter released "240 Bars (Spider Joke)" and "100 Bars (The Funeral)" attacking G-Unit and Loc. Jackson's response was "Not Rich, Still Lyin'", mocking The Game.<sup id="cite_ref-240Bars_273-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240Bars-273">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup> Lloyd Banks replied to the Game on a <i><a href="/wiki/Rap_City_(BET_program)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rap City (BET program)">Rap City</a></i> freestyle-booth segment, followed by a Game "diss" song ("SoundScan") ridiculing the 13-position drop of Banks' album <i>Rotten Apple</i> on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 chart and its disappointing second-week sales. Banks replied on his mixtape <i>Mo' Money In The Bank Pt. 5: Gang Green Season Continues</i> with "Showtime (The Game's Over)", said that Jackson wrote half of <i>The Documentary</i> and ridiculed The Game's suicidal thoughts.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In October 2006, The Game made a peace overture (which was not immediately answered) to Jackson,<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup> but two days later he said on <a href="/wiki/KPWR" title="KPWR">Power 106</a> that the peace offer was valid for only one day.<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup> In several songs on <i>Doctor's Advocate</i>, he implied that the feud was over. He said in July 2009 that the feud had ended with help from <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sean_Combs" title="Sean Combs">Diddy</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup> and apologized for his actions.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Tony_Yayo" title="Tony Yayo">Tony Yayo</a>, neither Jackson nor G-Unit accepted his apology<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup> and The Game has resumed his calls for a "G-Unot" boycott at concerts. Jackson released "So Disrespectful" on <i><a href="/wiki/Before_I_Self_Destruct" title="Before I Self Destruct">Before I Self Destruct</a></i>, targeting Jay-Z, The Game and <a href="/wiki/Young_Buck" title="Young Buck">Young Buck</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup> The Game responded with "Shake", poking fun at the music video for Jackson's "<a href="/wiki/Candy_Shop" title="Candy Shop">Candy Shop</a>".
</p><p>On January 2, 2015, The Game claimed that he and 50 were "sworn enemies", promising never to reconcile with him anymore,<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup> but on August 1, 2016, they ended their twelve-year feud when the two were in the Ace of Diamonds strip club and The Game said "I love 50, man. What happened, that shit was 12 years ago."<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2022, the feud reiterated after 50 critiqued Game's <i>Drink Champs</i> interview with <a href="/wiki/N.O.R.E." title="N.O.R.E.">N.O.R.E.</a>, where he claimed that 50's former competitor Kanye West did "more for me in two weeks than [Dr.] Dre did for me throughout my entire career".<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup> The Game responded, commenting that he enclosed the entirety of G-Unit as a group and clothing brand "in a casket", also expressing his likeliness in the <a href="/wiki/Power_(TV_series)" title="Power (TV series)"><i>Power</i></a> television trilogy, but warning 50 to "leave [the past] alone or else... I'm outside #Numinati".<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup> Then, two months later, in March, 50 Cent published a video via Instagram of Game being shunned by former Interscope Records CEO <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Iovine" title="Jimmy Iovine">Jimmy Iovine</a> at a basketball game, poking fun of it while also commenting "50 wrote ya hits". The Game once again flamed 50 after the claims were brought back up and also bragged to "get [50's] girlfriend out of my DM's".<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup> This was believed to have been a consequential result of Game claiming on <i>Drink Champs</i> to be "the best and a better rapper" than Eminem, with whom 50 still remains close friends.<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup> Additionally, Game's manager, Wack 100, has subliminally called out or questioned 50 Cent's credibility, over the rapper's surprise appearance at the <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_LVI" title="Super Bowl LVI">Super Bowl LVI</a> halftime show and ghostwriting allegations.<sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Cam.27ron"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Cam'ron">Cam'ron</span></h3>
<p>Jackson's issues with former <a href="/wiki/The_Diplomats" title="The Diplomats">Diplomat</a> <a href="/wiki/Cam%27ron" title="Cam&#39;ron">Cam'ron</a> began in 2007, when they had a live argument on <i>The <a href="/wiki/Angie_Martinez" title="Angie Martinez">Angie Martinez</a> Show</i> on <a href="/wiki/WQHT" title="WQHT">Hot 97</a> radio. Jackson commented that he felt that the music division of <a href="/wiki/Koch_Entertainment" title="Koch Entertainment">Koch Entertainment</a> (known today as <a href="/wiki/MNRK_Music_Group" title="MNRK Music Group">MNRK Music Group</a>) was a "graveyard", meaning major record labels would not work with their artists.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_292-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-292">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup> Cam'ron then ridiculed the record sales of G-Unit members Lloyd Banks and <a href="/wiki/Mobb_Deep" title="Mobb Deep">Mobb Deep</a> by pointing out that <a href="/wiki/The_Diplomats" title="The Diplomats">Dipset</a> member <a href="/wiki/Jim_Jones_(rapper)" title="Jim Jones (rapper)">Jim Jones</a> outsold both of their albums despite not being signed to a major label, and also went on to clarify that his group, The Diplomats, had a distribution deal from several labels.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_292-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-292">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup> Both rappers released diss songs with videos on <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a>. Jackson released "Funeral Music", and suggested in the song that Cam'ron is no longer able to lead The Diplomats and that Jim Jones should take his place. Cam'ron responded with "Curtis" and "Curtis Pt. II", in which he makes fun of not only Jackson's first name, but also his appearance, calling him "a gorilla, with rabbit teeth". Jackson responded by releasing "<a href="/wiki/Hold_On_(Young_Buck_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hold On (Young Buck song)">Hold On</a>" with <a href="/wiki/Young_Buck" title="Young Buck">Young Buck</a>. Since 2009, the feud slowly died down, and they eventually reconciled in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rick_Ross">Rick Ross</span></h3>
<p>Although <a href="/wiki/Rick_Ross" title="Rick Ross">Rick Ross</a> began a feud with Jackson over an alleged incident at the <a href="/wiki/2008_BET_Hip_Hop_Awards" title="2008 BET Hip Hop Awards">2008 BET Hip Hop Awards</a>, Jackson told news sources he did not remember seeing Ross there.<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">&#91;293&#93;</a></sup> Later that month Ross' "<a href="/wiki/Deeper_Than_Rap" title="Deeper Than Rap">Mafia Music</a>" was leaked on the Internet, with lyrics apparently disparaging Jackson. Several days later, Jackson released "Officer Ricky (Go Head, Try Me)" in response to "Mafia Music". The following day, Ross appeared on Shade 45 (Eminem's Sirius channel) and told Jackson to come up with something better in 24 hours.
</p><p>Before leaving for Venezuela, Jackson uploaded a video ("Warning Shot") and the first of a series of "Officer Ricky" cartoons. In early February he uploaded a YouTube video in which he interviewed "Tia", the mother of one of Ross' children; according to her, Ross is in reality a <a href="/wiki/Prison_officer" title="Prison officer">correctional officer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup> On February 5, 2009, The Game phoned Seattle radio station <a href="/wiki/KUBE_(FM)" class="mw-redirect" title="KUBE (FM)">KUBE</a>. Asked about the dispute between Jackson and Ross, he sided with Jackson and offered to mediate: "Rick Ross, holla at your boy, man" and "50 eating you, boy."<sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">&#91;295&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On his album <i><a href="/wiki/Deeper_Than_Rap" title="Deeper Than Rap">Deeper Than Rap</a></i>, Ross refers to Jackson in "In Cold Blood" and Jackson's mock funeral is part of the song's video. When the song was released, Ross said that he ended Jackson's career.<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup> "Rick Ross is Albert From <a href="/wiki/CB4" title="CB4">CB4</a>. You ever seen the movie? He's Albert," Jackson replied in an interview. "It never gets worse than this. You get a guy that was a correctional officer come out and base his entire career on writing material from a drug dealer's perspective such as <a href="/wiki/%22Freeway%22_Rick_Ross" class="mw-redirect" title="&quot;Freeway&quot; Rick Ross">"Freeway" Ricky Ross</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">&#91;297&#93;</a></sup> Their feud rekindled at the 2012 BET Hip Hop Awards, where Jackson and G-Unit members Kidd Kidd, Mike Knox, Tony Yayo were seen on video attacking <a href="/wiki/Gunplay_(rapper)" title="Gunplay (rapper)">Gunplay</a> (a member of Ross' Maybach Music Group). Gunplay's Maybach Music diamond necklace was stolen during the brawl, and several days later Jackson appeared at a Washington, D.C. bowling alley wearing Gunplay's chain.<sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">&#91;298&#93;</a></sup> On January 30, 2013, Jackson tweeted that Ross' attempted drive-by shooting on his birthday three days earlier was "staged".<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">&#91;299&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Jay-Z_and_Beyonc.C3.A9"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Jay-Z_and_Beyoncé">Jay-Z and Beyoncé</span></h3>
<p>In 1999, with the release of the single "<a href="/wiki/How_to_Rob" title="How to Rob">How to Rob</a>" 50 Cent attacked his rap peers, including Jay-Z. The latter responded to the provocation in the single "It's Hot (Some Like It Hot)" in which he says in one verse "Go against Jigga yo ass is dense/I'm about a dollar – what the f*ck is 50 Cents?".<sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">&#91;300&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In a 2009 interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i>, 50 Cent accused Jay-Z and his record company <a href="/wiki/Roc-A-Fella_Records" title="Roc-A-Fella Records">Roc-A-Fella Records</a> of being unfair to <a href="/wiki/Beanie_Sigel" title="Beanie Sigel">Beanie Sigel</a> because "[Jay-Z] didn't have their interests in mind, he was just doing what he had to do for himself." The rapper also stated that "I don't know him personally, [...] I tried to collaborate with him on the <a href="/wiki/Freeway_Ricky_Ross" title="Freeway Ricky Ross">Freeway</a> project ... What I did was Freeway went out and found his publishing deal, and we started the album. [...] when it came time to put the record out, he didn't want to shoot his video. He has a <a href="/wiki/God_complex" title="God complex">god complex</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">&#91;301&#93;</a></sup> 50 cent also accused Jay-z of changing in attitude and becoming meidatically more comparable since he married <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyoncé">Beyoncé</a>.
</p><p>In 2017 50 Cent reviewed Jay-Z's thirteenth <a href="/wiki/Album" title="Album">studio album</a> <i><a href="/wiki/4:44" title="4:44">4:44</a></i> defined it a "golf course music", stated in a <a href="/wiki/Instagram" title="Instagram">Instagram</a> post that "I listened to Jay sh*t, that <i>4:44</i>. [...] [It] was too smart. I felt like I was supposed to be wearing like glasses and shit and like a tie, a fucking sweater around my waist. It was like Ivy League. They don't wanna hear that shit. [...] They just wanna have a good time. You know what I'm saying? You can't be the best rapper at 47 because the new n****s is here. They coming with new [music] going on."<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">&#91;302&#93;</a></sup> In an interview on the <a href="/wiki/Conan_(talk_show)" title="Conan (talk show)"><i>Conan Show</i></a> , 50 Cent spoke about the album, saying: "Hip-hop culture's connected to youth culture. The kids gonna bring new innovative stuff. He just had the maturity bleed off into the material. [...]  But the kids, I don't see them actually listening to it".<sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">&#91;303&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305">&#91;304&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In an interview in 2022, 50 Cent reported that in a meeting between him and the couple in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>, the two rappers were having a heated argument. Beyoncé, seeing them, jumped from a ledge to come to her husband's defense. 50 Cent compared the singer to her sister <a href="/wiki/Solange_Knowles" title="Solange Knowles">Solange</a> when she hit Jay-Z in the elevator, describing them as "two gangstas".<sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306">&#91;305&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307">&#91;306&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In an interview for <a href="/wiki/XXL_(magazine)" title="XXL (magazine)"><i>XXL Mag</i></a> in 2023, 50 Cent claimed that Jay-Z's <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Awards" title="Grammy Awards">Grammy</a> wins were due to his marriage to Beyoncé:"Even Jay-Z's career, you can look at that and say the association to Beyoncé is when he started to receive the 16, 17 Grammys, since he's been with Beyoncé. And you go, prior to that [he had] one. That came with the association."<sup id="cite_ref-308" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-308">&#91;307&#93;</a></sup> 50 Cent also pointed out that the couple's eldest child <a href="/wiki/Blue_Ivy_Carter" title="Blue Ivy Carter">Blue Ivy Carter</a> won a Grammy even though she does not sing or rap, accusing award ceremonies of giving accolades to the couple just to ensure their attendance during the show.<sup id="cite_ref-309" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-309">&#91;308&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-310" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-310">&#91;309&#93;</a></sup> The rapper also reported that his non-win at the Grammys was due to his music being "a little bit abrasive to conservatives; [...] It didn't matter to me in that time period. Don't give me the trophy. They didn't give me Best New Artist and I sold 13 million records", while the Carter-Knowles family is more politically agreeable to the music industry.<sup id="cite_ref-311" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-311">&#91;310&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_nominations">Awards and nominations</span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_50_Cent" title="List of awards and nominations received by 50 Cent">List of awards and nominations received by 50 Cent</a></div>

<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/G-Unit_discography" title="G-Unit discography">G-Unit discography</a></div>

<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-5">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Sometimes abbreviated <b>Fiddy</b>, reflecting his own <a href="/wiki/AAVE" class="mw-redirect" title="AAVE">AAVE</a> pronunciation of "50". On <i><a href="/wiki/Late_Night_with_Seth_Meyers" title="Late Night with Seth Meyers">Late Night with Seth Meyers</a></i>, he advised "white people who are trying to be cool" to pronounce "50" as "fifty" rather than "fiddy".<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> </span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
